فلو صلى فرضاً، ذاكراً فائتة؛ ولو وتراً، فَسَدَ فرضه فساداً موقوفاً. فإن صلى خمس صلوات متذكراً في كلها تلك المتروكة قبل صلاتها وخرج وقت الخامسة مما صلاه بعد المتروكة، ذاكراً لها صحت جميعها عند أبي حنيفة لأن الحكم وهو: الصحة، مع العلة وهي: الكثرة، يقترنان والكثرة صفة هذا المجموع، لأن الفاسد في حكم المتروك فكانت المتروكات ستاً حكماً، وحكمها سقوط الترتيب، فإذا ثبتت صفة الكثرة بوجود الأخيرة، استندت الصفة إلى أولها بحكمها، فتجوز الكل التي صلاها، كأنه سقط الترتيب من أول صلاة تركها، ولا بد من سقوط الترتيب على وجه لا يضاف إلى الأخيرة فقط، فإن العلة لو كانت هي الأخيرة لثبت الحكم مقتصراً، فوجب أن يثبت مستنداً ليكون الحكم مضافاً إلى الكثرة التي هي العلة، دون الأخيرة التي ليست علة، فلم يجب الترتيب من الأصل، ولا يمتنع توقف حكم على أمر آخر حتى يتبين حاله، كتعجيل الزكاة إلى الفقير، يتوقف كونها فرضاً على تمام الحول والنصاب التام، فإن تم على نمائه كان التعجيل فرضاً، وإلا كان نفلاً، وكمغرب مزدلفة في طريقها المعتاد، موقوف على عدم إعادتها قبل الفجر، فإن أعادها كانت نفلاً، وإلا كانت فرضاً، وارتفع الفساد، وظهر الجمعة وصلاة المعذور إذا انقطع عذره فيها، والناقص على عادة الحيض إذا صلت بعد انقطاعه، فإذا سعى إلى الجمعة، وانقطع العذر وقتاً كاملاً، وعاد دمها، بطلت صلاتهم، وإلا تعين صحتها فلا تَبْطُلُ الخمس التي صلاها متذكراً للفائتة بقضاء الفائتة المتروكة بعده أي: بعد خروج وقت الخامسة لسقوط الترتيب، وإن قَضَى الفائتة المتروكة قبل خروج وقت الخامسة مما صلاه متذكراً لها، بَطَلَ وَصْفُ ما صلاه متذكراً للفائتة قبلها أي: قبل قضائها، وصار الذي صلاه نفلا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وعند محمد بطل أصلها، فلا تنتقض الطهارة بقهقهته فيها عنده خلافاً لهما رحمهم الله.
If he prays a current fard prayer while remembering a missed prayer, even if it is witr, his fard prayer becomes invalid with a conditional invalidity. Then if he prays five prayers, remembering that missed prayer before each prayer, and the time of the fifth prayer (from those performed after the missed prayer) exits while he remembers it, all five become valid according to Abu Hanifa, because the ruling (validity) and the cause (multiplicity) are concurrent, and multiplicity is an attribute of this total. For the invalid prayer is in the ruling of the missed one, so the missed prayers become six in effect, and their ruling is that order is dropped. When the attribute of multiplicity is established by the existence of the last one, the attribute is attributed to the first one by its ruling, so all that he prayed are permissible, as if order was dropped from the first prayer he missed. It is necessary that the dropping of order is not attributed only to the last one, for if the cause were the last one, the ruling would be limited, so it must be established as based on the multiplicity which is the cause, not the last one which is not the cause, so order was not obligatory from the beginning. There is no impossibility in a ruling being suspended on another matter until its condition becomes clear, like the acceleration of zakat to the poor: its being fard is suspended on the completion of the year and full nisab, if it continues to increase, the acceleration becomes fard, otherwise it becomes nafl; and like the Maghrib of Muzdalifah on the usual path, it is suspended on not repeating it before dawn, if he repeats it, it becomes nafl, otherwise it becomes fard, and the invalidity is removed; and like the validity of Friday prayer and the prayer of the excused person if his excuse ceases during it, and the prayer of the woman with irregular menstruation after it stops; if he goes to Friday prayer and the excuse ceases for a complete time, and her blood returns, their prayers become invalid, otherwise validity is determined. So the five prayers he performed while remembering the missed prayer are not invalidated by making up the missed prayer after it, i.e., after the time of the fifth has exited, because order is dropped. And if he makes up the missed prayer before the time of the fifth exits from those he performed while remembering it, the attribute of what he performed remembering it becomes invalid, i.e., before making it up, and what he performed becomes nafl according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; according to Muhammad, its essence becomes invalid, so purity is not broken by laughing in it according to him, contrary to them.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on praying a current fard prayer while remembering a missed prayer. The base ruling is that if one begins a current fard prayer while remembering a missed prayer (including witr), the current prayer becomes invalid with a conditional invalidity (fasād mawqūf). This means the invalidity is not final; it may be resolved or confirmed depending on subsequent actions. The text explains the condition for resolution: if the person continues praying five more prayers (the current and subsequent ones) without repeating the missed prayer, and the time of the fifth such prayer (after the missed one) expires while still remembering the missed prayer, then all five prayers become valid according to Abu Hanifa. The reasoning is that the effective cause (illa) for dropping the obligation of order (tartib) is multiplicity (kathrah). When the number of missed prayers (including the invalid ones) reaches six in effect, the obligation of order is dropped retroactively from the first prayer. This is likened to other cases where a ruling is suspended, such as advance payment of zakat or the Maghrib prayer at Muzdalifah. The passage then clarifies the consequence if the missed prayer is made up before the time of the fifth expires: the attribute of being a valid fard prayer is lost, and the prayers become nafl according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf; however, Imam Muhammad holds that they become completely invalid (batil), with the practical effect that laughing in prayer does not break wudu according to him. This difference highlights the nature of conditional invalidity: for Muhammad, the invalidity is absolute once the missed prayer is performed before the condition is met.

Key Terms
فساد موقوف (fasād mawqūf): Conditional invalidity: an invalidity that is not final but depends on a future event; if the event occurs, the invalidity is confirmed; if not, the prayer becomes valid.
الترتيب (al-tartib): The obligation to pray missed prayers in order before current prayers; when missed prayers accumulate to six, this obligation drops.
كثرة (kathrah): Multiplicity; the cause for dropping the order requirement when the number of missed prayers (including invalid ones) reaches six.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person prays a current fard prayer while remembering a missed prayer, and then prays five more prayers without making up the missed one, when do these five prayers become valid according to Abu Hanifa?
A) Immediately after the sixth prayer
B) When the time of the fifth prayer (after the missed one) expires
C) When all five are completed
D) When the missed prayer is made up

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi concept of conditional invalidity (fasād mawqūf) shows that rulings can be suspended on future conditions, and multiplicity (kathrah) of missed prayers can retroactively validate the order.

Praying While Remembering a Missed Prayer: Nafl or Batil?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tarteeb and the condition of the fifth prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayers performed while remembering a missed prayer, distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and apply the condition of the fifth prayer's time exit.

Core Idea
If you pray while remembering a missed prayer, your prayer becomes nafl, not invalid, provided the fifth prayer's time exits.

What happens if you remember a missed prayer while you are already praying a current prayer? Does your prayer become invalid, or does it count as something else? The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on this question, with Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf ruling that the prayer becomes nafl, while Imam Muhammad rules it becomes batil. The key condition is the exit of the time of the fifth prayer. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the reasoning and the precise condition, clarifying common misconceptions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the main ruling for the majority of the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the prayer performed while remembering a missed prayer becomes nafl, not batil. This is the mufta bihi position.
The prayer loses the description of fard but remains valid as nafl.
2
Identify the opposing view
Imam Muhammad holds that the prayer becomes batil entirely. This means it is as if it was not performed, and effects like laughing with qahqaha do not break wudu (since the prayer is already void).
Muhammad's view is based on a stricter application of qiyas.
3
Understand the condition of the fifth prayer
According to the passage, the crucial factor is the exit of the time of the fifth performed prayer after the missed one. If after the missed prayer you pray five prayers and the time of the fifth exits, then those five prayers become valid as nafl. If the fifth time has not exited, the invalidity is still pending.
The common expression that 'the sixth prayer validates the five' is a simplification; the real validator is the exit of the fifth time.
4
Analyse the proofs
Abu Hanifa uses istihsan: since order is waived when missed prayers reach six, there is no need to invalidate all. Muhammad uses qiyas on the case of starting prayer in ample time and prolonging it: that prayer is not valid, so here also the order violation invalidates.
The Hanafi response is that the analogy is flawed because tarteeb involves multiple prayers and istihsan removes hardship.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Abu Hanifa, if you pray five prayers after the missed one and the fifth time exits, you only need to make up the missed one. According to Muhammad, you must make up both the missed and all five performed prayers.
This difference affects both the number of qada prayers and whether laughing in those prayers breaks wudu.

المبسوط»: إن المصححة للخمس هي السادسة، بأنه غير صحيح ليس كما ينبغي، نعم لو قال: هي مظهرة، فلما كانت مظهرة للصحة أضيفت إليها لكان حسناً، كما قد علمته والله الحمد.
The missed (prayer), before the exit of the time of the fifth, the description of what he prayed while remembering before it becomes void, and it becomes nafl. It: the missed (prayer) before the exit of the time of the fifth from what he prayed while remembering it, (the description becomes void) not the essence (of what he prayed while remembering) the missed prayer (before it), i.e. before its qada, (and) it does not remain described as fard, but (becomes) what he prayed (nafl) according to Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf, and according to Muhammad its essence becomes void, so wudu is not broken by laughter in it according to him, contrary to them, may Allah have mercy on them. Note: we specified lifting the invalidity by the exit of the time of the fifth from the performed prayers after the missed one, because that is the verification in the ruling of the issue, and what is mentioned in most books like al-Hidayah, al-Nihayah, al-Inayah, Ghayat al-Bayan, al-Kafi, and al-Tabyin, that the transformation of all into permissible is dependent on performing six prayers after the missed one, is only meant to emphasize the exit of the time of the fifth from the performed prayers, not a condition of performing the sixth, nor even the entry of its time; because the exit of time does not necessitate the entry of another, as if the fifth of the performed prayers is Fajr and the sun rises, as we verified in our hashiah on al-Durar wa al-Ghurar. Then Allah informed me by [؟] on its agreement and its text. Then know that the condition for correcting the five is that the missed prayers become six by the exit of the time of the fifth, which is the sixth of the missed, not the performance of the sixth before qada of the missed necessarily. But they mentioned performing the sixth, which is the seventh of the missed, to make the missed prayers six with certainty, not that it is a condition at all. End. And he said in Majma' al-Riwayat: Then know that the invalidity of prayer by abandoning order is suspended according to Abu Hanifah, may Allah have mercy on him. If they become many and the invalid ones together with the missed become six, its validity appears, otherwise not, as in accelerating zakat, performing Zuhr before Jumu'ah, and cessation of blood before the habit. And according to them, the invalidity is definite so he must make up the missed prayers in every case, by analogy to if one began prayer while time was ample and he prolonged it until time became narrow, it does not become permissible by consensus. End. And he said in al-Tatar Khaniyyah: A man left Zuhr and prayed six prayers after it while remembering the missed, only the missed is due according to the Imam, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: he makes up the missed and five after it; because they say the invalidity is definite not suspended. And if he prayed five prayers after the missed, then he made up the missed, meaning in the time of the fifth, the statement would be: he must repeat the five he prayed in all their sayings. End. Because if after the exit of the time of the fifth, the Imam would not say the necessity of repetition. And in al-Sighnaqi: If he prayed the sixth before engaging in qada, the five are valid according to him, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi said: This is what is said: one invalidates five and one validates five. End. So the missed invalidates the five, i.e., it confirms their invalidity by his performing it in the time of the fifth of the performed prayers, and the sixth of the performed prayers validates the five before it, and in reality the validator is the exit of the time of the fifth, but because it is necessary from the exit the entry of a prayer time and its performance in it mostly, mentioning its performance is substituted for the entry of its time. End. And Qadi Khan said after the above: Likewise, if one left five prayers and then prayed one prayer after them while remembering that he did not pray the five, then he prays the five and repeats the sixth in all their sayings. If he did not make up the missed and did not repeat the sixth until he prayed the seventh while remembering what he did, the seventh becomes permissible in their sayings, and he must make up the five missed, and they differed regarding the sixth. Abu Hanifah said: He does not repeat the sixth, and they said: He repeats the sixth. Abu Hanifah made a distinction: before the exit of the time of the sixth he repeats the sixth, and after the exit of its time he does not repeat; because before the exit of the time of the sixth the missed are five, so order is not waived, but after the exit of the time of the sixth, if repeating the sixth were obligatory, the missed would be six, so order would be waived, so the repetition is waived. End. So these texts match the research of al-Muhaqqiq Kamal ibn al-Humam, and this which we said is more appropriate than the statement of the author of al-Bahr, may Allah have mercy on him: 'The correct is to say...' etc., since their statement is not wrong, as you know. Likewise, his ruling on the statement of the author of al-Mabsut: 'The validator of the five is the sixth' as being incorrect is not as it should be. Yes, if he said: 'It is a manifestor,' then since it is a manifestor of validity it is attributed to it, it would be good, as you know. And praise be to Allah.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of praying while remembering a missed prayer (fā'itah). The core issue is whether such prayers become invalid (bāṭil) or merely lose the description of farḍ and become nafl. The author clarifies the condition of the fifth prayer after the missed one. According to Imam Abū Ḥanīfah and Abū Yūsuf, if a person prays a present prayer while remembering a missed prayer, that present prayer does not become invalid; rather, it becomes nafl. However, Imām Muḥammad holds that it becomes invalid entirely (baṭala aṣluhā), meaning it is as if it was not performed, and thus laughing with qahqaha in it does not invalidate wuḍū', contrary to the other two. The author emphasizes that the key factor is the exit of the time of the fifth performed prayer after the missed one. If after praying the missed prayer, the person continues to pray five valid prayers, then the exit of the time of the fifth after the missed one 'validates' the previous prayers (i.e., they are considered permissible as nafl). If the fifth time has not exited, the invalidity is still pending. The author refutes the notion that performing a sixth prayer is necessary; rather, the condition is merely the exit of the fifth time. He supports this with quotes from various scholars like Ṣadr al-Sharī'a, al-Sarakhsī, Qāḍīkhān, and others, showing that the relied-upon position is that of Imām Abū Ḥanīfah with the condition of the exit of the fifth time.

Key Terms
المتروكة (al-matrukah): The missed prayer (fā'itah) that was not performed in its time.
الخامسة (al-khāmisah): The fifth performed prayer after the missed one; its time exit is the condition for validity of the previous prayers.
ترتيب (tarteeb): The obligation to perform prayers in their prescribed order: first qada of missed then present.
نفل (nafl): A supererogatory prayer, not obligatory; here it describes prayers that were intended as fard but become nafl due to missing order.
فساد (fasād): Invalidity of prayer; according to Muhammad, the prayer is completely invalid (bāṭil).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the status of prayers performed while remembering a missed prayer, once the time of the fifth performed prayer after the missed one has exited?
A) They become invalid (batil) and must be repeated.
B) They become nafl (supererogatory).
C) They remain fard and are valid.
D) They become invalid only if the missed prayer was Zuhr.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, prayers performed while remembering a missed prayer become nafl (not invalid) once the time of the fifth such prayer exits, based on istihsan.

Intention for Many Missed Prayers and Fasting: Specification (Ta'yīn) and the Two Corrections
Explains the method of making intention for missed prayers when many are due.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on specification (ta'yīn) in intention for multiple missed prayers and fasting, and distinguish between the two correct opinions concerning the need for specification in fasting.

Core Idea
For many missed prayers, intending the first or last of each type covers the rest; for fasting, two correct views exist on whether specification is needed.

When a person has accumulated numerous missed prayers, specifying each one individually can be burdensome. The Hanafi school provides a facilitation: one may intend the first or last missed prayer of that type, and the intervening ones are automatically fulfilled. The same principle applies to fasting from multiple Ramadans, though there is an ikhtilaf (difference of opinion) on the need for specification. In this lesson, we will parse the text from Imdad al-Fattah to understand the ruling and the two corrections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central issue
The passage deals with intention (niyyah) when one has many missed prayers (fawā'it) of the same type.
2
Extract the ruling for prayer
The text states that to facilitate, one may intend the first or the last of the missed prayers (e.g., 'first Zuhr upon him' or 'last Zuhr'). This specification covers all in between.
3
Recognize the two corrections for fasting
For fasting from two Ramadans, there are two correct opinions (tas-hihan mukhtalifan): (a) al-Zayla'i's view that specification is necessary and can be done via first/last, and (b) al-Khulasa's view that specification is not needed at all.
4
Note the tarjih (preference)
The author declares the prayer ruling (with specification via first/last) as 'the most correct' (al-aṣaḥḥ). For fasting, no explicit tarjih is given; both corrections are presented.
5
Observe the incomplete textual quote
The passage ends with a quote from al-Kanz that is cut off; note that the full ruling may require cross-referencing.

And when the missed prayers become many, he needs to specify each prayer. So if he wants to make the matter easy for himself, he intends the first Zuhr upon him, or the last of it, and likewise fasting from two Ramadans according to one of two different corrections. Commentary
This passage addresses the issue of making intention (niyyah) when a person has many missed prayers (fawā'it) of the same type, e.g., multiple Zuhr prayers missed over several days. The author states that normally one must specify each prayer by its time, day, etc. But to ease the burden, one may intend either the first or the last of the missed prayers of that type. For example, if one has missed several Zuhr prayers, he can intend 'the first Zuhr upon me' or 'the last Zuhr upon me.' This works because by specifying the boundary, the intervening ones are automatically included. The same rule applies to fasting when one has missed days from two different Ramadans: according to one correct opinion, specification is necessary and can be done by intending 'the first day' or 'the last day.' Another correction (from al-Khulasa) says that specification is not necessary at all for fasting; simply intending 'qada of what I owe from the two months' suffices. The author states that the ruling for prayer (the necessity of specification via first/last) is the more correct (al-aṣaḥḥ). The passage ends abruptly with a quote from al-Kanz.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yīn): Specification of the exact prayer (e.g., 'Zuhr of such date') in intention.
أول ظهر عليه (awwal zuhr 'alayhi): The earliest Zuhr prayer that one missed; specifying it covers all subsequent missed Zuhr prayers.
آخر ظهر عليه (ākhir zuhr 'alayhi): The latest Zuhr prayer that one missed; specifying it covers all previous missed Zuhr prayers.
تصحيحان مختلفان (taṣḥīḥān mukhtalifān): Two differing correct opinions within the Hanafi school regarding the need for specification in fasting.

Specification of Many Missed Prayers and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Order
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ta'yin and tartib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ta'yin for many missed prayers and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding order when a sixth prayer is performed.

Core Idea
Ta'yin is wajib for many missed prayers; order drops when missed prayers exceed five.

This lesson addresses a practical scenario: a person has many missed prayers (fawa'it) and wants to make them up. The Hanafi school requires specification (ta'yin) but offers an easement: intend the first or last of the type. A deeper dispute arises when a person with five missed prayers then prays the current prayer (the sixth). Does the sixth need to be repeated? Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ based on how the obligation of order (tartib) operates when the number exceeds five. Understanding this ikhtilaf helps you apply the correct fatwa in qada situations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making up many missed prayers (qada al-fawa'it). The matn states that ta'yin (specification) is needed when prayers are numerous. Determine that this is a wajib requirement but with an easement.
The number 'many' here means more than one; the specific threshold for dropping order is six.
2
State the facilitative method
The text provides that one may intend the first or last of the missed prayers of that type (e.g., first Zuhr or last Zuhr) and that will count as valid specification. Understand that this avoids the difficulty of specifying each prayer individually.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Qadhi Khan presents a scenario: five missed prayers, then a sixth (current prayer) is performed. Abu Hanifa says: before the time of the sixth exits, repeat it; after its time, no repeat. Sahibayn say: always repeat. The key is whether the missed prayers become six, which drops order according to Abu Hanifa.
The ikhtilaf is about the effect of exceeding five on the obligation of tartib.
4
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if the sixth's time has exited, Abu Hanifa does not require repetition, while the Sahibayn do. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is Abu Hanifa's, supported by the commentator and Ibn al-Humam.
Fatwa today follows Abu Hanifa's differentiation.

Source Text

(وإذا كثُرَتِ الفوائتُ) ولو كانت لازمة الترتيب فليس المراد الكثرة المسقطة للترتيب، بل مطلق الكثرة فحينئذ (يحتاج لتعيين كل صلاة) عند قضائها لتزاحم الفروض والأوقات التي هي أسباب، كقوله: أصلي ظهر الخميس عاشر الحجة سنة خمس وأربعين وألف) وهذا فيه كلفة فإذا أراد تسهيل الأمر عليه نـوى أول ظهـر عـلـيـه) فإذا نواه وصلاه كذلك فما يليه يصير أولاً، فيصح بمثل تلك النية، وهكذا (أو) إن شاء نوى (آخره) أي: آخر ظهر عليه فإذا نواه وصلاه كذلك فما يليه يصير آخراً بالنظر لما كان فيحصل التعيين بيقين.
When missed prayers become many, he needs to specify each prayer. If he wants to make the matter easy for himself, he may intend the first noon prayer upon him or the last. The five prayers are validated by the prayer before them, and in reality, the validator is the exit of the time of the fifth, but since the exit necessarily entails the entry of a prayer time and performance in it generally, mentioning its performance is made to stand in place of its time entry. End. Qadhi Khan said: Also if he left five prayers and then prayed a prayer after them, remembering that he had not prayed the five, then he prays the five and repeats the sixth according to their statement. If he did not make up the missed prayers and did not repeat the sixth until he prayed the seventh, remembering what he had done, the seventh is valid in their statement, and he must make up the five missed prayers, and they differed about the sixth. Abu Hanifa said: he does not repeat the sixth. The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: he repeats the sixth. Abu Hanifa differentiated: before the time of the sixth leaves, he repeats the sixth; after its time leaves, he does not repeat, because before the time of the sixth leaves the missed prayers are five, so order is not dropped; after the time of the sixth leaves, if repeating the sixth were obligatory, the missed prayers would become six, so order is dropped, so the repetition drops. End. So these texts match the research of the investigator Kamal ibn al-Humam, and this statement of ours is more appropriate than the statement of the author of al-Bahr: the correct is to say... etc., since their statement is not wrong as you have learned. Also his ruling on the statement of the author of al-Mabsut: that the validator of the five is the sixth, that it is incorrect, is not proper. Yes, if he said: it is a manifestor, then since it is a manifestor of validity it is attributed to it, it would be good, as you have learned. And praise be to Allah. (And when missed prayers become many) even if they are subject to order, the meaning is not the great number that drops order, rather absolute abundance, then (he needs to specify each prayer) when making them up due to the crowd of obligations and times which are causes, like his saying: I pray the noon prayer of Thursday, the 10th of Dhu al-Hijja, year 1145. This has difficulty. If he wants to make the matter easy for himself, he intends the first noon prayer upon him, so if he intends and prays it thus, what follows it becomes first, so it is valid with such intention. Similarly, he may intend the last noon prayer upon him, so if he intends and prays it thus, what follows it becomes last relative to what was, so specification is achieved with certainty.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the ruling on specification (ta'yin) when a person has many missed prayers (fawa'it) and wishes to make them up (qada). The base text (matn) establishes that when missed prayers are numerous, one must specify each prayer individually, but for ease one may intend either the very first or the very last of the missed prayers of that type (e.g., Zuhr) and that will serve as valid specification. The commentator then expands by explaining that the validation of the five prayers (i.e., making up all five missed prayers) is achieved by performing the fifth prayer, but the real validator is the exit of its time. He quotes Qadhi Khan, who presents a scenario: a person misses five prayers, then prays a sixth prayer (i.e., the prayer due at that time) while remembering the missed ones. According to the majority (Sahibayn), he must pray the five and also repeat the sixth. But if he delays and prays the seventh without making up, the seventh is valid but he still owes the five. The dispute concerns the sixth: Abu Hanifa holds that if he prays the sixth before its time exits, he must repeat it; if after its time exits, he does not repeat it, because repeating it would make the total missed prayers six, and the order (tartib) is dropped when prayers exceed five, thus the repetition is not required. The Sahibayn hold that the sixth must always be repeated. The commentator sides with Ibn al-Humam, indicating that the preferred view follows Abu Hanifa, and criticizes the author of al-Bahr for calling the Mabsut position incorrect. Finally, the commentary restates the matn, adding that the requirement for ta'yin applies even if the prayers are subject to order, and the easement of intending first or last suffices.

Key Terms
الفوائت (al-fawa'it): Missed obligatory prayers (or fasts) that must be made up (qada).
التعيين (al-ta'yin): Specification of the identity of a missed prayer, e.g., by date and time, to ensure proper qada.
الترتيب (al-tartib): The obligation to make up missed prayers in chronological order (e.g., Fajr before Zuhr before Asr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Three
B) Four
C) Five
D) Six or more

Key Takeaway
Ta'yin is wajib for many missed prayers but facilitated; tartib drops when the count reaches six, affecting the need to repeat a sixth prayer after its time.

Excusing a New Muslim in Dar al-Harb for Missed Obligations
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute and ancillary qada rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether a new Muslim in dar al-harb must perform qada for missed worship, and evaluate the dissent of Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
A new Muslim in dar al-harb is excused; knowledge is a condition for liability.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a person who embraces Islam in enemy territory is liable for missed obligatory acts of worship. The majority holds that he is excused because the divine address (khitab) only binds when one has knowledge or its evidence. Imam Zufar dissents, analogizing to the obligation of faith. We will analyze the evidence, the response, and the practical consequences, then explore related rulings on qada delays and uncertainty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The core case: a person accepts Islam in dar al-harb and was ignorant of the obligations of prayer, zakat, etc. The ruling: he is excused for the period of ignorance; no qada is required.
Contrast with a Muslim in dar al-Islam who is not excused.
2
Trace the legal basis (dalil)
The majority argues that the divine address (khitab) only becomes binding when the person has knowledge of it or its evidence. Since the new Muslim lacked such knowledge, he is not liable.
This is based on the usul principle that obligation requires capacity (taklif) which includes knowledge.
3
Examine Zufar's dissent
Imam Zufar imposes liability for missed obligations, analogizing to the obligation of faith (iman). He argues that just as faith is known through reason and ignorance does not excuse, the same applies to specific shar'i obligations.
Zufar's position is a minority view within the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The commentator rejects the analogy: the existence of the Creator is self-evident, but the specific obligations (e.g., five daily prayers) require revelation and are not known by reason alone. Thus, ignorance of them is excusable.
This highlights a distinction between innate knowledge (fitrah) and revealed commandments.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to the majority, no qada is required for missed acts before knowledge. According to Zufar, the new Muslim must perform all missed prayers, fasts, etc.
This difference has significant practical implications for converts.
6
Consider related rulings
The passage also addresses: (a) an apostate must only make up the prayer whose time remains and hajj; (b) delaying qada for an excuse like family provision is permissible; (c) if one does not know how many prayers were missed, he acts on his best guess or prays until certain.
These rulings expand the discussion on liability and concession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُعْذَرُ مَنْ أسلم بدار الحربِ بِجَهْلِهِ الشَّرائِعَ ) أي : الأحكام الواجبة من افتراض الصلاة والزكاة والصـوم والحج ونحوها مدة جهله؛ لأن الخطاب إنما يلزم بالعلم به أو بدليله، ولم يوجـد، بـخـلاف المسلم بـدار الإسلام، وألزمه بها زفر كما يلزمه الإيمان، قلنا: دليل وجود الصانع ) ظاهر ، فلا يـعـذر بجهله، وليـس عنده دليل على وجود فرض الصلاة ونحوها فيعذر، وإذا ارتد المسلم والعياذ بالله تعالى- حبطت أعماله، ولا يلزمه إلا قضاء الصلاة التي بقي وقتها والحج لبقاء السبب، كما في «الفتح». تنبيه: سنذكر حكم قضاء السنة وفي كشف الأسرار : أن المثلية في القضاء لإزالة المآثم، ثم لإحراز الفضيلة قال «صاحب البحر » : والظاهر أن المراد بالمآثم إثم ترك الصلاة فلا يعاقب عليها إذا قضاها، وأما إثم تأخيرها عن الوقت الذي هو كبيرة فباق لا يزول بالقضاء المجرد عن التوبة بل لا بد منها. انتهى. وفي ( المعراج » : قال في المجتبى»: الأصح أن تأخير قضاء الفوائت بـعــذر السعي على العيال، وفي الحوائج، يجوز قيل: وإن وجب على الفور يباح له التأخير، وعن «أبـي جعفر » : سجدة التلاوة، والنذر المطلق وقضاء رمضان، موسع ، وضيّق ( الحلواني» والـعــامـري، والطحاوي خلافهما، وذكر الولوالجي في الصوم أن قضاء الصوم على التراخي، وقضاء الصلاة على الفور إلا لعذر. انتهى. وفي ( الحاوي»: لا يدري كمية الفوائت يعمل بأكبر رأيه، فإن لم يكن له رأي يقضي حتى يستيقن، واختلف فيما يقضى احتياطاً فقيل : يقرأ السورة في الأخيريين مع الفاتحة وقيل: الفاتحة فقط كما في « الدراية».
And excused is the one who accepts Islam in dar al-harb due to his ignorance of the shari'a, i.e., the obligatory rulings of prayer, zakat, fasting, hajj and the like, during the period of his ignorance; because the address (khitab) only becomes binding by knowledge of it or its evidence, and it did not exist, contrary to the Muslim in dar al-Islam. And Zufar imposed it upon him just as he imposes faith. We said: the evidence for the existence of the Creator is apparent, so he is not excused for ignorance of it, but he has no evidence for the existence of the obligation of prayer etc., so he is excused. And if a Muslim apostatizes, his deeds are annulled, and only the qada of prayer whose time remains and hajj is obligatory upon him due to the persistence of the cause, as in al-Fath. Note: we will mention the ruling on qada of sunnah. And in Kashf al-Asrar: that the similarity in qada is to remove the sins, then to attain virtue. The author of al-Bahr said: apparently what is meant by sins is the sin of leaving prayer, so he is not punished for it if he makes it up; as for the sin of delaying it from its time, which is a major sin, it remains and is not removed by mere qada without repentance, rather repentance is necessary. End. And in al-Mi'raj: it is said in al-Mujtaba: the more correct is that delaying the qada of missed prayers due to an excuse of striving for family and needs is permissible. It is said that even though it is obligatory immediately, delay is permissible for him. And from Abu Ja'far: the prostration of recitation, absolute vow, and qada of Ramadan are expanded (mucad), and al-Halwani and al-Amiri and al-Tahawi restricted contrary to them. And al-Walwaliji mentioned in fasting that the qada of fasting is with delay (tarakhi) and the qada of prayer is immediate except for an excuse. End. And in al-Hawi: if he does not know the quantity of missed prayers, he acts on his best guess; if he has no opinion, he prays until he is certain. And they differed about what to pray cautiously: it is said that he recites the surah in the last two rak'ahs with the Fatiha; and it is said: the Fatiha only, as in al-Diraya.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage covers several related rulings concerning qada (make-up) of missed acts of worship. The core ruling is that a person who accepts Islam in dar al-harb (enemy territory) is excused for not performing the obligatory acts of worship during the period of his ignorance, because the divine address (khitab) only becomes binding when one has knowledge of it or its evidence. By contrast, a Muslim in dar al-Islam is not excused. The text notes that Zufar (a Hanafi imam) held a dissenting view, making the new Muslim liable for the missed obligations, analogizing to the obligation of faith. The commentator rejects this, arguing that the evidence for the existence of the Creator is evident, but evidence for the specific obligations of prayer, etc., is not, so he is excused. The passage then addresses apostasy: if a Muslim apostatizes, his good deeds are annulled, but he must still make up any prayer whose time remains (i.e., the current prayer time) and hajj, because their cause (sabab) persists. A note follows about qada of sunnah prayers, quoting from Kashf al-Asrar that qada is meant to remove sin, but the sin of delaying a prayer beyond its time (a major sin) is only removed by repentance, not mere qada. Then the text discusses the ruling on delaying qada: the more correct view is that if one delays making up missed prayers due to an excuse like earning a living for the family, it is permissible, though immediate qada is obligatory. The passage then records a disagreement among Hanafi scholars about whether qada of Ramadan fasts is immediate or delayed, with al-Walwaliji stating that fasts are with delay (tarakhi) while prayers are immediate unless excused. Finally, it addresses the case of someone who does not know how many prayers he missed: he should act on his best guess, and if he has no idea, he must pray until he is certain. Regarding the recitation in the make-up prayers, there is a difference of opinion: some say recite a surah in the last two rak'ahs along with Fatiha, others say only Fatiha.

Key Terms
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim rule where Islamic law is not enforced.
الخطاب (al-khitab): The divine address (command or prohibition) from Allah, which is the basis of obligation.
السعي على العيال (al-sa'y 'ala al-'iyal): Striving to provide for one's family; considered a valid excuse for delaying qada of prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A new Muslim in dar al-harb is excused for missed obligatory acts of worship if he was ignorant of them, because liability requires knowledge of the divine address or its evidence.

Excuse for Ignorance for a New Muslim in Dar al-Harb
Ruling on excuse for ignorance and Zufar's ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a new Muslim in dar al-harb is excused for missed obligations due to ignorance and explain the response to Zufar's opposing view.

Core Idea
A new Muslim in dar al-harb is not liable for missed obligations due to ignorance of the laws.

When a person embraces Islam in a non-Muslim land (dar al-harb), he may not have been aware of the detailed obligations of the faith. The Hanafi school holds that he is excused for the period of his ignorance because liability requires knowledge of the ruling or its evidence. However, Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing that just as belief in the Creator is known by reason, so are the obligations. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position and the proof behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Determine the exact ruling: a new Muslim in dar al-harb is excused for missed obligations (prayer, zakah, fasting, hajj) during his ignorance. Note that this applies only in dar al-harb, not dar al-Islam.
2
Locate the opposing view
Identify Zufar's position that the new Muslim is not excused and must make up all missed obligations.
Zufar is a Hanafi imam, making this an intra-Hanafi dispute.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Understand the dalil aqli: the obligation of prayer, etc., requires a revealed proof (nass), which the new Muslim lacked. In contrast, belief in the Creator is proven by reason, so ignorance of that is not excused.
The text states: 'the evidence for the existence of the Creator is apparent, so he is not excused for ignorance of it, and he has no evidence for the existence of the obligation of prayer and the like, so he is excused.'
4
Consider the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to the Hanafi view, the convert does not need to make up missed acts; according to Zufar, he would need to make up everything.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُعْدَرُ مَنْ أسلم بدار الحربِ بِجَهْلِهِ الشَّرائِعَ. (۲) نوی قضاء رمضان ولم يعين اليوم [ صح ] ، ولو عن رمضانين، كقضاء الصلاة صح، وإن لم ينو أول صلاة أو آخر صلاة عليه. انتهى. قال شارحه الزيلعي هذا قول بعض المشايخ، والأصح أنه يجوز في رمضان واحد، ولا يجوز في رمضانين ما لم يعين أنه صائم عن رمضان سنة كذا، وكذا في قضاء الصلاة انتهى. وفي « الخلاصة : إذا وجب عليه قضاء يومين من رمضان واحد، ينبغي في القضاء أن ينوي أول يوم وجب عليه قضاؤه من هذا الرمضان، وإن لم يعين الأول يجوز، وكذا لـو كــان عـلـيـه قـضـاء يـومـيـن مـن رمضانين وهو المختار، ولو نوى القضاء لا غير يجوز ، وإن لم يعين، وكذا في قضاء الصلوات. انتهى. ويُعْذَرُ مَنْ أسلم بدارِ الحربِ بِجَهْلِهِ الشّرائِعَ ) أي : الأحكام الواجبة من افتراض الصلاة والزكاة والصـــوم والحج ونحوها مدة جهله؛ لأن الخطاب إنما يلزم بالعلم به أو بدليله، ولم يوجـد، بـخـلاف المسلم بـدار الإسلام، وألزمه بها زفر كما يلزمه الإيمان، قلنا: دليل وجود الصانع ) ظاهر ، فلا يـعـذر بجهله، ولـيـس عنده دليل على وجود فرض الصلاة ونحوها فيعذر، وإذا ارتد المسلم والعياذ بالله تعالى- حبطت أعماله، ولا يلزمه إلا قضاء الصلاة التي بقي وقتها والحج لبقاء السبب، كما في «الفتح». تنبيه: سنذكر حكم قضاء السنة وفي كشف الأسرار : أن المثلية في القضاء لإزالة المآثم، ثم لإحراز الفضيلة قال «صاحب البحر » : والظاهر أن المراد بالمآثم إثم ترك الصلاة فلا يعاقب عليها إذا قضاها، وأما إثم تأخيرها عن الوقت الذي هو كبيرة فباق لا يزول بالقضاء المجرد عن التوبة بل لا بد منها. انتهى. وفي ( المعراج » : قال في المجتبى»: الأصح أن تأخير قضاء الفوائت بـعــذر السعي على العيال، وفي الحوائج، يجوز قيل: وإن وجب على الفور يباح له التأخير، وعن «أبـي جعفر » : سجدة التلاوة، والنذر المطلق وقضاء رمضان، موسع ، وضيّق ( الحلواني» والـعــامــري، والطحاوي خلافهما، وذكر الولوالجي في الصوم أن قضاء الصوم على التراخي، وقضاء الصلاة على الفور إلا لعذر. انتهى. وفي ( الحاوي»: لا يدري كمية الفوائت يعمل بأكبر رأيه، فإن لم يكن له رأي يقضي حتى يستيقن، واختلف فيما يقضى احتياطاً فقيل : يقرأ السورة في الأخيريين مع الفاتحة وقيل: الفاتحة فقط كما في « الدراية».
One is excused who embraces Islam in dar al-harb due to his ignorance of the laws. (2) He intended to make up Ramadan but did not specify the day [it is valid], even if for two Ramadans, like making up prayer it is valid, even if he did not intend the first prayer or the last prayer due on him. End. Its commentator al-Zayla'i said this is the saying of some mashayikh, but the more correct is that it is permissible for one Ramadan, and not permissible for two Ramadans unless he specifies that he is fasting for Ramadan of such a year, and similarly for making up prayer. End. And in al-Khulasah: If making up two days from one Ramadan is obligatory on him, it is appropriate in making up that he intend the first day that was obligatory to make up from this Ramadan, and if he does not specify the first it is permissible, and similarly if he had to make up two days from two Ramadans, and this is the chosen view. And if he intends making up only, it is permissible even without specifying, and similarly for making up prayers. End. And one who embraces Islam in dar al-harb is excused due to his ignorance of the laws, i.e., the obligatory rulings such as the obligation of prayer, zakat, fasting, hajj and the like, for the duration of his ignorance. Because the address is only binding by knowledge of it or its evidence, and it is not present, contrary to a Muslim in dar al-Islam. Zufar held him liable as he is liable for faith. We say: the evidence for the existence of the Creator is apparent, so he is not excused for ignorance of it, and he has no evidence for the existence of the obligation of prayer and the like, so he is excused. And if a Muslim apostatizes – Allah forbid – his deeds are nullified, and nothing is obligatory on him except making up the prayer whose time remained and hajj due to the survival of the cause, as in al-Fath. Note: We will mention the ruling on making up sunnah. And in Kashf al-Asrar: That similitude in making up is to remove sins, then to attain virtue. The author of al-Bahr said: And the apparent is that what is meant by sins is the sin of leaving prayer, so he is not punished for it if he makes it up. As for the sin of delaying it beyond its time, which is a major sin, it remains, not removed by mere making up without repentance, rather repentance is necessary. End. And in al-Mi'raj: He said in al-Mujtaba: The more correct is that delaying the making up of missed prayers due to the excuse of striving for one's dependents and in necessary matters is permissible. It is said: even if it is obligatory immediately, he is permitted to delay. And from Abu Ja'far: Sajdah al-Tilawah, the absolute vow, and making up Ramadan are broad. And al-Halwani, al-Amiri, and al-Tahawi held the opposite. And al-Welwaliji mentioned regarding fasting that making up fasting is with leniency, and making up prayer is immediate except for an excuse. End. And in al-Hawi: If one does not know the quantity of missed prayers, he acts on his best judgment. If he has no opinion, he makes up until he is certain. And they differed as to what he makes up as a precaution: it is said he recites a surah in the last two rak'ahs with al-Fatihah, and it is said: only al-Fatihah, as in al-Dirayah.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah covers two main themes: the ruling on excusing a new Muslim in dar al-harb for ignorance of shar'i obligations, and the details of intention (niyyah) when making up missed fasts of Ramadan. The commentator expands on the base text of Nur al-Idah, presenting multiple Hanafi opinions and choosing the relied-upon position. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute since it involves differences among Hanafi scholars (e.g., al-Zayla'i, the author of al-Khulasah, and others). The core rule is that one who accepts Islam in dar al-harb is not held liable for the obligations he missed during his ignorance because he lacked knowledge and the means to acquire it. Zufar's opinion to the contrary is rejected because the evidence for the existence of Allah is clear, but the specific obligations are not. The discussion also covers the rule of apostasy nullifying deeds but requiring qada' of missed acts with remaining causes. Regarding niyyah, the preferred view is that for missed fasts from the same Ramadan, specifying the first day is commendable but not obligatory; for missed fasts from different Ramadans, specification is necessary. The passage also touches on the delay of qada' due to livelihood excuses, and the need for repentance to remove the sin of delaying.

Key Terms
عذر (‘udhr): A legal excuse that exempts one from liability for missed obligations due to ignorance or inability.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): A non-Muslim land where Islamic law is not enforced and Muslims may not have free access to religious knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi justification for excusing a new Muslim in dar al-harb from missed acts of worship?
A) He was not accountable at all before embracing Islam.
B) He lacked access to the revealed evidence for those obligations.
C) The obligations of worship are not binding on non-Muslims.
D) He can make up the missed acts after learning.

Key Takeaway
A new Muslim in dar al-harb is excused for missed obligations due to ignorance because liability requires knowledge or evidence.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Intention for Qada' of Ramadan Fasts
Intra-Hanafi dispute on specification in niyyah for qada'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the need to specify the day when making intention for qada' of missed fasts, and differentiate the ruling for fasts from one Ramadan vs. multiple Ramadans.

Core Idea
For qada' of missed fasts, general intention suffices even for multiple Ramadans, according to the preferred view.

When making up missed fasts of Ramadan, does one need to specify the exact day or year in the intention? The Hanafi school has an internal difference. Al-Zayla'i held that specification is required for fasts from two different Ramadans, but the author of al-Khulasah and the chosen (mukhtar) view hold that a general intention to perform qada' is sufficient. This lesson explores this dispute and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making intention (niyyah) for qada' of missed Ramadans. The ruling is that it is wajib to intend qada', but the issue is whether specification is necessary.
2
State the base text opinion
The base text of Nur al-Idah says that if someone intends qada' of Ramadan without specifying the day, it is valid (sahh), even for two Ramadans.
This is the default ruling in the matn.
3
Present al-Zayla'i's objection
Al-Zayla'i in his commentary says the correct view is that it is valid for one Ramadan but not for two Ramadans without specifying the year.
He claims this is the 'asahh' (more correct).
4
Present the view of al-Khulasah
Al-Khulasah states that for two days from one Ramadan, it is permissible not to specify the first day; for two days from two Ramadans, specification is not required either. This is called al-mukhtar (the chosen view).
This view generalizes to qada' of prayers as well.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage indicates that the view of al-Khulasah is the chosen (mukhtar) and thus the operative position for fatwa.
Therefore, general intention is sufficient in all cases.

Source Text

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Cutting Solitary Prayer to Join Congregation
Ruling on a person who starts a fard prayer alone then cuts it to join the congregation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting a solitary fard prayer to join the congregation, identify the proof (dalil) and the condition (mahall al-rafd), and distinguish the preferred view from the alternative within the madhhab.

Core Idea
Cutting a solitary fard prayer for congregation is sunnah muakkadah before the prayer is bound.

What should you do if you begin a fard prayer alone and then the congregation for the same prayer begins? This lesson examines the Hanafi position that it is recommended to cut the solitary prayer and join the congregation. We will explore the proof from hadith, the underlying principle of 'cutting for completion,' and a subtle intra-madhhab disagreement about the timing of the cut.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is starting a fard prayer alone and then cutting it to join a congregation. According to the correct view (al-sahih), the ruling is that cutting is sunnah muakkadah—recommended but not obligatory.
The hukm level is derived from the superiority of congregational prayer.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the well-known hadith: 'Salat al-jama'ah tafdulu salata al-fadhdhi bi-khamsin wa 'ishrina darajah' (congregational prayer is superior to solitary prayer by twenty-five degrees). This hadith establishes the greater merit of congregation.
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning, so thubut is qati'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit statement of superiority indicates that joining the congregation is more meritorious. Thus, cutting the lesser act (solitary prayer) to obtain the greater act is justified. The Law permits nullifying a worship for a superior one, analogously to demolishing a mosque to rebuild it better.
This is a form of istihsan: preferring the stronger evidence.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Shams al-A'imma suggested that one should pray two rak'ahs then cut to combine both merits. However, the preferred view (adopted by al-Hidayah and al-Tabyin) is immediate cutting because the person is in 'mahall al-rafd' (a position of abandonment before the prayer is tied).
The later authorities, including Fakhr al-Islam, inclined to immediate cutting.
5
Understand the principle of mahall al-rafd
The concept of mahall al-rafd refers to a state where an act of worship is not yet fully bound. Until the prayer is tied (by reaching the final sitting, for example), the Law grants the worshiper authority to abandon it for a superior act. This explains why cutting is permissible.
Analogies: cutting zuhr for jumu'ah, or a thorn in sujud causing a pause.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب إدراك الفريضة مع الإمام وغيره
إذا شَرَعَ في فرض منفرداً، فأُقِيمَتِ الجماعةُ قَطَعَ، واقتدى .
باب إدراك الفريضة مع الإمام وغيره
وحقيقة هذا الباب مسائل شتّى تتعلق بالفرائض في الأداء الكامل ( إذا شَرَعَ) المصلي (في) أداء (فرض)، أو قضائه، (منفرداً، فأُقِيمَتِ الجماعةُ) في ذلك الفرض بأن أحــرم الإمام؛ لأن حقيقـة إقامة الشيء فعله، وهذا هو المراد لأنه بمجرد شروع المؤذن في الإقامة لا يقطع، بل يتم ركعتين بالإجماع، وإن لم يقيد بالسجود، ثم يقطع في الرباعية، فإذا شرع الإمام (قطع) المنفرد، بأن يسلم تسليمة واحدة قائماً (وَ) بعده (اقتدى) على الصحيح؛ لأنه بمحل الرفض. والقطع للإكمال إكمال معنى، فيجوز، كنقض المسجد لتجديده، وكنقض الظهر للجمعة ، وكمن أصاب جبهته شوك في سجوده فرفع ثم وضع لم يجعل سجدتين، كذا في ( البحر ) يعني: سجدتين مانعتين من زيادة ثالثة، فهما بمنزلة واحدة، إلا أنه لو أصابته الشوكة وقد أصابت جبهته الأرض فلم يطمئن ورفع رأسه لا لقصد الإكمال صحت سجدته، وقال في «معراج الدراية » : والقطع للإكمال يجوز كهدم المسجد للبناء يجوز على الوجه الأكمل، وكذا لو أصابته الشوكة في المسجد فرفع لسجدة أخرى يجوز لأنه للإكمال. انتهى. والأصل أن نقض العبادة قصداً بلا عذر حرام لقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلَا تُبْطِلُوا أَعْمَلَكُمْ [ : ٣٣] ولإفضائه إلى السفه، وإذا كان القطع ثم الإعادة من غير زيادة إحسان جائزاً لحطام الدنيا كالمرأة إذا فار قدرها، والمسافر إذا ندت دابته، أو غيره أو خاف فوت درهم من مال، فجوازه لتحصيله [ نفسه ] على وجه أكمل أولى بالجواز، لأن « صَلاةُ الجَمَاعَةِ تَفْضُلُ صَلَاةَ الفَدَّ بِخَمْسٍ وَعِشْرِينَ دَرَجَةً»، وفي رواية ( بِسَبْعِ وَعِشْرِينَ دَرَجَةً )، وتقييدنـا القـطـع بـأنـه عـلـى الصحيح تبعـاً للهداية»، و « التبيين»، وإليه مال فخر الإسلام، احترازاً عـمـا مـال إليه شمس الأئمة: أن يصلي ركعتين ثم يقطع؛ لأنه يمكنه الجمع بين الفضيلتين، والصحيح أنه يقطع لأنه بمحل الرفض، ولهذا لو قام المسبوق لقضاء ما سبق به وسجد الإمام للسهو، عليه أن يتابع الإمام ويترك تلك الركعة، ولو سجد الإمام بعدما قيد السجدة، لا يتابع إمامه حتى لو تابعه وسجد معه تفسد صلاته، ولــو قـام لخامسة له رفض القيام ويعود إلى القعدة، فعلم أن الشرع جعل له ولايـة الـرفـض قبل التقييد
Chapter on Attaining the Obligatory Prayer with the Imam and Others. When he commences a fard prayer alone, then the congregation is started, he cuts it and joins. Chapter on Attaining the Obligatory Prayer with the Imam and Others. And the reality of this chapter is various matters relating to obligatory prayers in complete performance. (When the praying person commences) to perform (fard), or its qada', (alone, then the congregation is started) in that fard by the Imam entering ihram, because the reality of establishing something is doing it, and this is what is meant, because with the mere start of the mu'adhdhin in the iqamah, he does not cut; rather he completes two rak'ahs by consensus even if not bound by sujud, then he cuts in a four-rak'ah prayer. When the Imam commences, the individual cuts by giving one salam while standing, and after that joins according to the correct view, because he is in a position of abandonment. And cutting for completion is a meaning of completion, so it is permissible, like demolishing a mosque to renew it, and like breaking the zuhr for jumu'ah, and like one who gets a thorn in his forehead during sujud and then raises then places: it is not considered two prostrations. Thus in al-Bahr, meaning: two prostrations that prevent a third, so they are like one, except that if the thorn gets him while his forehead is on the ground and he doesn't settle and raises his head not for the purpose of completion, his prostration is valid. And it is said in Mi'raj al-Dirayah: And cutting for completion is permissible, like demolishing a mosque to rebuild it in a more perfect manner, and similarly if a thorn gets him in the mosque and he raises for another prostration, it is permissible because it is for completion. End. And the principle is that intentionally nullifying an act of worship without an excuse is haram due to His statement 'Do not nullify your deeds' and because it leads to foolishness. And if cutting and then redoing without increase of excellence is permissible for trivial worldly matters, like a woman if her pot boils over, or a traveler if his mount runs away, or if he fears losing a dirham of money, then its permissibility to attain it [himself] in a more perfect manner is more deserving of permissibility, because 'prayer in congregation is superior to prayer alone by twenty-five degrees' and in a narration 'by twenty-seven degrees'. And we restrict the cutting to being on the correct view following al-Hidayah and al-Tabyin, to which Fakhr al-Islam inclined, as a precaution against what Shams al-A'imma inclined to: that he should pray two rak'ahs then cut, because he can combine both merits. The correct view is that he cuts because he is in a position of abandonment. Therefore, if a latecomer stands to make up what he missed and the Imam prostrates for forgetfulness, he must follow the Imam and leave that rak'ah; and if the Imam prostrates after tying the prostration, he does not follow his Imam, and if he follows and prostrates with him, his prayer is invalidated. And if he stands for a fifth rak'ah, he must abandon the standing and return to sitting. Thus it is known that the Law has given him the authority of abandonment before tying.
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage is the opening of a new chapter in Imdad al-Fattah on the ruling when a person begins a fard prayer alone and then a congregation begins. The commentator expands on the matn of Nur al-Idah, providing detailed proof and analogies. The main ruling: if a person starts a fard prayer (or its qada') alone, and then the congregation for that same prayer starts (by the Imam entering ihram), it is recommended for the individual to cut his prayer (by giving one salam while standing) and join the congregation. This is the correct view (al-sahih). The rationale is that cutting for a more complete act is itself a form of completion, analogous to demolishing a mosque to rebuild it better, or breaking the zuhr prayer to join jumu'ah. The proof includes the hadith on the superiority of congregational prayer. The passage also distinguishes between cutting before the prayer is 'tied' (i.e., before an essential part is bound) and after; before tying, cutting is permissible. Shams al-A'imma suggested praying two rak'ahs then cutting, but the preferred view is immediate cutting because the individual is in a state of abandonment (mahall al-rafd). Examples of cutting for worldly needs are given to show that if cutting is allowed for trivial reasons, it is even more allowed for religious excellence.

Key Terms
القطع للإكمال (al-qat‘ li al-ikmal): Cutting one act of worship to perform a more complete version of the same or another act.
محل الرفض (mahall al-rafd): A state in which an act of worship can be abandoned before it is legally 'tied' (i.e., before a binding element like the final sitting).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in this passage, when should a person who has started a fard prayer alone cut it to join the congregation?
A) After completing two rak'ahs.
B) Immediately when the Imam begins the congregation (enters ihram).
C) Only if he has not yet performed any ruku'.
D) After the iqamah is called, regardless of the Imam's start.

Key Takeaway
It is sunnah muakkadah to cut a solitary fard prayer and join the congregation for the same prayer, provided the cut occurs before the prayer becomes tied (pre-tashahhud).

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Cutting One's Prayer to Join the Congregation
Ruling on cutting a solitary obligatory prayer to join congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting a solitary obligatory prayer to join the congregation and identify the conditions under which cutting is required or not.

Core Idea
Cutting an obligatory prayer to join the congregation is permissible and even required, because congregational prayer's superiority outweighs the partial loss.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains when a person who has started an obligatory prayer alone should cut it to join the congregation. The Hanafi school permits this based on the principle of abandoning a lesser good for a greater one, supported by the hadith on the superiority of congregational prayer. We will examine the ruling, its conditions, and an internal Hanafi difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Read the opening lines: When one begins an obligatory prayer alone and the congregation is established (imam starts), he cuts his prayer and follows the imam. This is the primary ruling.
Cutting is done by giving one salutation while standing.
2
Note the conditions
The passage lists several conditions: the prayer must be obligatory (not supererogatory), the congregation must be for the same prayer in the same location, and the person must not have prostrated in the first rak'ah of a four-rak'ah prayer. If prostrated, he adds a second rak'ah to make it voluntary.
If the congregation is in a different place (e.g., home vs. mosque), cutting is not allowed.
3
Analyze the proof
The proof includes the hadith that congregational prayer is 25 or 27 times superior to individual prayer, and analogies like demolishing a mosque to rebuild it better.
The principle is that cutting for a more complete form of worship is permissible.
4
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
Shams al-A'imma held that one should pray two rak'ahs first to combine benefits, but the correct (mufta bihi) view is immediate cutting.
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) favor immediate cutting.
5
Apply to concrete scenarios
Work through the variations: four-rak'ah prayer with or without prostration, two-rak'ah (Fajr), three-rak'ah (Maghrib), and supererogatory prayers.
For Maghrib, the majority rule of the whole applies, so cutting is allowed after prostration.

قَوْمٍ، فَصَلِّيَا مَعَهُمْ)
Chapter on Catching the Obligatory Prayer with the Imam and Others
When one begins an obligatory prayer alone, and the congregation is established, he cuts (his prayer) and follows (the imam).
Chapter on Catching the Obligatory Prayer with the Imam and Others
The reality of this chapter is various issues related to obligatory prayers in complete performance. (When) the praying person (begins) the performance of (an obligatory prayer), or its make-up, (alone, and the congregation is established) for that obligatory prayer, meaning the imam has entered the prayer (because the reality of establishing a thing is doing it), and this is what is meant, because merely the caller starting the iqama does not necessitate cutting; rather he completes two rak'ahs by consensus, even if not bound by prostration, then he cuts in a four-rak'ah prayer. So when the imam begins (the prayer), the solitary person cuts (his prayer) by giving one salutation while standing, and (after that) he follows (the imam) according to the correct view, because he is in a state of abandonment. Cutting for completion is a meaningful completion, so it is permissible, like demolishing a mosque for its renovation, and like abandoning the zuhr for the jumu'a, and like the case of one who gets a thorn on his forehead during prostration, then raises (his head) and places (it again), it is not counted as two prostrations. Thus in al-Bahr: meaning two prostrations that prevent a third; so they are like one. However, if the thorn pricks him after his forehead has touched the ground and he did not have composure and raised his head without intending completion, his prostration is valid. And he said in Mi'raj al-Diraya: Cutting for completion is permissible, like demolishing a mosque for building, permissible in the most complete manner. Similarly, if the thorn pricks him in the mosque and he raises for another prostration, it is permissible because it is for completion. End. The original principle is that deliberately nullifying worship without excuse is prohibited due to His saying: 'And do not invalidate your deeds' [33] and because it leads to foolishness. And if cutting and then repeating without additional goodness is permissible for worldly matters - like a woman whose pot boils over, or a traveler whose animal runs away, or other such things, or one who fears losing a dirham of his wealth - then its permissibility for attaining (himself) in the most complete manner is even more clearly permissible, because 'the prayer in congregation surpasses the prayer of an individual by twenty-five degrees' and in another narration 'twenty-seven degrees.' And we restricted the cutting to being on the correct view following al-Hidaya and al-Tabyin, and Fakhral-Islam leaned towards it, as a precaution against what Shams al-A'imma inclined to: that he prays two rak'ahs then cuts, because he can combine both merits. The correct view is that he cuts because he is in a state of abandonment. For this reason, if a latecomer stands to make up what he missed and the imam prostrates for forgetfulness, he must follow the imam and leave that rak'ah. And if the imam prostrates after binding the prostration, he does not follow his imam, and if he were to follow and prostrate with him, his prayer would be invalid. And if he stands for a fifth (rak'ah), he must abandon the standing and return to sitting. So it is known that the Law has given him the authority of abandonment before binding by prostration, and cutting for completion is completion. And because if he swore not to pray, he would not be considered sworn for less than a rak'ah, as in al-Diraya, al-Fath, and al-Inaya. Then he restricted the cutting by his saying: (If he has not prostrated for what he began) of the first rak'ah, whether the prayer is four-rak'ah or not, (or he has prostrated) for the first rak'ah (in a non-four-rak'ah prayer), such as Fajr or Maghrib, then he cuts after prostration as well with one salutation, because if he were to add another rak'ah to a two-rak'ah prayer, he would miss the congregation since he would have completed the whole (prayer), and there is no voluntary prayer after Fajr; and the majority in Maghrib have the ruling of the whole, and one does not perform voluntary prayer in it as a follower as we will mention. And we restricted it to beginning an obligatory prayer, because if he were in a supererogatory prayer, he does not cut until he completes it in pairs. And a vowed prayer is like an obligatory one. And we restricted it to the congregation being established in the place of his performance. So if he was praying at home, for example, and the congregation is established in the mosque, or in the mosque and it is established in another mosque, he does not cut at all, as mentioned by al-Marghinani. And if he begins a supererogatory prayer and a funeral (prayer) is held, and he fears that if he does not cut it he will miss it, he cuts because he cannot combine both benefits. Cutting a supererogatory prayer has a substitute in making it up, unlike the funeral prayer; if he chooses to miss it, it has no substitute. So in al-Fath, and this indicates the permissibility of cutting an obligatory prayer as well to combine two benefits. (And if he has prostrated) and it was (in a four-rak'ah prayer), like Zuhr, (he adds a second rak'ah) to protect what he has performed from invalidity, and recites the tashahhud (and gives salutation, so that the two rak'ahs become a voluntary prayer for him, then he follows (the imam) as someone performing an obligatory prayer) to attain the merit of congregation. (And if he had prayed three rak'ahs) of a four-rak'ah prayer and the congregation is established, (he completes it) as four rak'ahs alone. Al-Zayla'i said: From Muhammad that he completes it sitting so that his prayer turns into a supererogatory prayer, then he prays with the congregation to combine the reward of the voluntary and the reward of the congregation in the obligatory. The apparent view is that the majority has the ruling of the whole, so it does not admit of nullification. (Then) after its completion, (he follows as a volunteer) if he wishes, and this is better, to attain through it the merit of congregation in Zuhr and Isha, because voluntary prayer after them is permissible, even behind an imam and it is not disliked, because it is not in a manner of summoning as we have mentioned. And if he wishes, he does not perform a voluntary prayer, because people have a choice in it. The better is to follow as a volunteer, because it is prescribed in Zuhr and Isha, and if he leaves it in these (prayers), perhaps he may be accused of not holding congregation (as valid). And it is narrated: (That the Prophet, peace be upon him, when he finished Zuhr, saw two men in the back rows who had not prayed with him. He said: 'Bring them here.' So they came, their shoulder blades trembling. He said: 'Take it easy, for I am the son of a woman who used to eat dried meat.' Then he said: 'What prevented you from praying with us?' They said: 'We had prayed in our dwellings.' He said, peace be upon him: 'When you pray in your dwellings, then come to the prayer of a people, pray with them.)
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and detailed conditions from the Hanafi school on cutting a solitary obligatory prayer to join the congregation. The central ruling: if a person begins an obligatory prayer alone and then the congregation for that same prayer is established (meaning the imam has begun the prayer), he should cut his prayer and join. The author clarifies that the cutting is done by giving one salutation while standing, and then he follows the imam. This is based on a principle: cutting for a more complete form of worship is allowed, analogous to demolishing a mosque to rebuild it better or leaving the Zuhr prayer for Friday prayer. The proof includes the hadith that congregational prayer is twenty-five or twenty-seven times superior. The passage addresses a difference within the Hanafi school: Shams al-A'imma held that one should pray two rak'ahs and then cut, because by doing so he combines the reward of both the partial prayer and the congregation. The correct view (as per al-Hidayah, al-Tabyin, and preferred by Fakhr al-Islam) is to cut immediately, because the solitary prayer is in a state of being abandoned (mahall al-rafd). The author then details conditions: (1) The prayer must be obligatory (not supererogatory). (2) The congregation must be established in the same place; if the person is praying at home and the congregation is at the mosque, he does not cut. (3) If he has not prostrated in the first rak'ah, he cuts immediately regardless of the type of prayer. If he has prostrated and the prayer is a two-rak'ah (Fajr) or three-rak'ah (Maghrib), he still cuts after prostration. If he has prostrated in a four-rak'ah prayer (Zuhr, Asr, Isha), he should complete a second rak'ah to make it a voluntary prayer in pairs, then give salutation, and then join the congregation as one performing an obligatory prayer. If he has already prayed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah prayer, he completes four rak'ahs alone, then may follow the imam as a volunteer (offering a supererogatory prayer). The passage ends with a hadith of the Prophet instructing two men who had prayed at home to pray again with the congregation as a supererogatory prayer. This shows the recommendation of performing a voluntary prayer to attain congregational reward when one has already prayed individually.

Key Terms
قطع (qat'): Cutting the prayer by giving salutation before completing it, to join the congregation.
إدراك (idrak): Catching the prayer with the imam, i.e., joining the congregation.
اقتدى (iqtada): Following the imam in prayer as a ma'mum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, when does a person who started an obligatory prayer alone NOT cut his prayer to join the congregation?
A) When he has prostrated in the first rak'ah of a four-rak'ah prayer
B) When he is praying at home and the congregation is at the mosque
C) When he is praying a supererogatory prayer
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
Cutting a solitary obligatory prayer to join the congregation is permissible and even required, based on the superiority of congregational prayer, except in specified conditions like after prostration in a four-rak'ah prayer or if the congregation is in a different location.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Cutting Short Optional Prayer When Congregation Begins
Explains when and how to cut short an optional prayer to join congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for cutting a nafl prayer when iqamah begins, apply them to two-rak'ah and four-rak'ah prayers, and evaluate the dispute about Fajr and Asr.

Core Idea
Cut a nafl only before prostration; after prostration, complete a pair, then join for fard — but not for Fajr, Asr, or Maghrib.

This lesson unpacks the detailed Hanafi rules for when you are in the middle of an optional prayer and the congregation starts. The ruling is not a simple 'cut or continue' — it depends on how many rak'ahs you have completed, whether you have prostrated, and which prayer you are in. We will also examine the hadith evidence and the key disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Determine whether in fard or nafl
If you have started a fard prayer (or a vowed prayer), the rules for cutting apply. If you are in a nafl, you should complete it in pairs (shaf'an) before joining the congregation.
A vowed prayer (nadhr) is treated like fard.
2
Check if you have prostrated in the current rak'ah
If you have not yet prostrated in the first rak'ah, you may cut immediately with one taslim, whether the prayer is four-rak'ah or not. This preserves the opportunity to join the congregation from the start.
This applies only if the iqamah is in the same place of prayer.
3
Apply the rule for non-four-rak'ah prayers after prostration
If you have already prostrated in a two- or three-rak'ah prayer (Fajr, Maghrib), you must cut with one taslim. You cannot add a rak'ah because that would turn it into a four-rak'ah, and nafl after Fajr/Maghrib is not allowed.
For Maghrib, completing it as four would cause conflict with the imam if you join later.
4
Apply the rule for four-rak'ah prayers after prostration
If you have prostrated in the first rak'ah of a four-rak'ah fard (Zuhr, Isha), add a second rak'ah to make a pair, perform tashahhud and taslim, then join the congregation as a muftarid (intending fard). This turns the two rak'ahs into a nafl.
The two rak'ahs are now a nafl, so you can later join the fard congregation.
5
Handle the case of having prayed three rak'ahs
If you have already completed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard, complete the fourth as fard alone. After finishing, you may optionally join the congregation as a mutanaffil (nafl follower) for Zuhr and Isha only. Imam Muhammad held a different view, but the mufta bihi is to complete as fard.
You cannot join as a mutanaffil for Fajr, Asr, or Maghrib because nafl is disliked in those times.
6
Understand the hadith proof and inter-madhhab dispute
The Prophet (peace be upon him) told two men who had prayed at home to join the congregation and make their prayer a nafl, except in Asr. The Hanafi school extends the exception to Fajr and Maghrib based on stronger hadiths. The Shafi'i school allows it in all times.
The Hanafi tarjih relies on the prohibition of nafl after Fajr and Asr, and the analogy for Maghrib.
