وهو أفضل؛ ليدرك بها فضيلة الجماعة في الظهر والعشاء، لجواز النفل بعدهما، ولو مع الإمام وليس مكروهاً؛ لأنه ليس على سبيل التداعي كما قدمناه، وإن شاء لا يتطوع لأن الناس فيه بالخيار، والأفضل الاقتداء متطوعاً؛ لأنه مشروع في الظهر والعشاء، وإذا تركه فيهما ربما يتهم أنه مما لا يرى الجماعة وروي : ( أنَّه عليه الصلاة و والسلام لَمَّا فَرَغَ مِنَ الظَّهْرِ رَأى رَجُلَيْنِ فِي أُخْرِيَاتِ الصُّفُوفِ لَمْ يُصَلِّيَا مَعَهُ، فَقَالَ: عَليَّ بِهِمَا، فَأَتَيَا وَفَرَائِصُهَمَا تَرْتَعِدُ، فَقَالَ: عَلَى رِسْلِكُمَا فَإِنِّي ابْنُ امْرَأَةٍ كَانَتْ تَأْكُلُ القَدِيْدَ، ثُمَّ قَالَ: مَا لَكُمَا لَمْ تُصَلِّيَا مَعَنَا؟ فَقَالَا: كُنَّا صَلَّيْنَا فِي رِحَالِنَا، فَقَالَ عليه الصلاة والسلام: إذا صَلَّيْتُمَا فِي رِحَالِكُمَا، ثُمَّ أَتِيْتُمَا صَلاةَ قَوْمٍ، فَصَلِّيَا مَعَهُمْ، إلا في العصر. وإن قام لثالثة، فأقيمت قبل سجودِهِ، قَطَعَ قائماً بتسليمة، في الأصح.. وَاجْعَلا صَلَا تَكُمَا مَعَهُمْ سَبْحَةٌ » (١) أي: نافلة، كذا في « العناية »، و « الدراية»، فإن قيل: روى أبو داود، والترمذي، والنسائي، عن يزيد بن الأسود الله قال : « شَهِدْتُ مَعَ النَّبيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم حَجَّتَهُ فَصَلَّيْتُ مَعَهُ صَلَاةَ الصُّبْحِ فِي مَسْجِدِ الْخَيْفِ، فَلَمَّا قَضَى صَلاتَهُ، إِذَا هُوَ بِرَجُلَيْنِ فِي أخْرَى القَوْمِ لَمْ يُصَلِّيَا مَعَهُ، فَقَالَ: عَلَيَّ بِهِمَا، فَجِيءَ بِهِمَا تَرْعَدُ فَرَائِصُهُمَا، قَالَ: مَا مَنَعَكُمَا أنْ تُصَلِّيَا مَعَنَا؟ قَالا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ إِنَّا كُنَّا صَلَّيْنَا فِي رِحَالِنَا، قَالَ فَلا تَفْعَلا إِذَا صَلَّيْتُمَا فِي رِحَالِكُمَا، ثُمَّ أَتَيْتُمَا مَسْجِدَ جَمَاعَةٍ، فَصَلِّيَا مَعَهُمْ، فَإِنَّهَا لَكُمَا نَافِلَةٌ » (۲) صححه الترمذي. فالجواب هو معارض بما تقدم من حديث النهي عن التنفـل بعد العصر والصبح، وهو مقدم لزيادة قوته؛ ولأن المانع مقدم، وفيه حديث صريح أخرجه الدارقطني عن ابن عمر أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : « إِذَا صَلَّيْتَ فِي أَهْلِكَ، ثُمَّ أدْرَكْتَ الصَّلاةَ فَصَلِّهَا، إِلَّا الفَجْرَ والمغرب» (۳) والأمر بالصلاة في غير هذين الوقتين للندب، والصارف للأمـر عـن الوجوب جعلها نافلة، (إلا) أنه لا يقتدي متنفلاً ( في العصر ) والفجر لكراهة النفل، وكراهته في المغرب لما يلزم مخالفة الإمام لو أتمها أربعاً، وإن وافقه لزم التنفل بالبتيراء كما سنذكره
If he does not prostrate for what he has begun, or he prostrates in a non-four-rak'ah prayer, and if he prostrates in a four-rak'ah prayer, he adds a second rak'ah, and makes taslim, so that the two rak'ahs become supererogatory for him, then he joins as one intending obligatory prayer. And if he has prayed three rak'ahs, he completes it, then joins as a supererogatory follower. With the prostration, and cutting for completion is completion, and because if he swore not to pray, he would not be in violation of his oath for less than a rak'ah, as in al-Dirayah, al-Fath, and al-Inayah. Then he restricted cutting with his statement: (If he does not prostrate for what he has begun) from the first rak'ah and the prayer is four or non-four, or he prostrates for the first rak'ah in a non-four, such as Fajr or Maghrib, then he cuts after prostration also with a salutation, because if he adds another rak'ah to the two-rak'ah prayer, he would miss the congregation due to completing everything, and one does not perform supererogatory prayers after Fajr, and the majority in Maghrib has the ruling of the whole, and one does not perform supererogatory prayer in it as a follower as we will mention. And we restricted it to having started a fard because if he were in a nafl, he does not cut until he completes it in pairs, and a vowed prayer is like a fard. And we restricted it to the iqamah being in the place of its performance; so if he was praying at home for example and iqamah was made in the mosque, or in the mosque and iqamah was made in another mosque, he does not cut at all, as mentioned by al-Marghinani. And if he began a nafl and a funeral arrived, and he fears missing it if he does not cut, he cuts because he cannot achieve both merits together, and cutting the nafl is followed by making it up, unlike the funeral; if he chose to miss it, it would be without replacement, as in al-Fath, and it indicates the permissibility of cutting the fard also to combine both merits. (And if he prostrates) and it was (in a four-rak'ah prayer) like Zuhr, (he adds a second rak'ah) to protect what has been performed from invalidity, and performs tashahhud (and makes taslim, so that the two rak'ahs become a nafl for him, then he joins as one intending fard) to achieve the virtue of congregation. (And if he has prayed three rak'ahs) of a four-rak'ah prayer and iqamah is made, (he completes it) as four alone. Al-Zayla'i said: And from Muhammad that he completes it sitting so that his prayer becomes nafl, then he prays with the congregation to combine the reward of nafl and the reward of congregation in the fard; the apparent view is that the majority has the ruling of the whole, so it does not bear abrogation. (Then) after his completion (he joins as a supererogatory follower) if he wishes, and that is better, to achieve the virtue of congregation in Zuhr and Isha, because nafl is permissible after them, and even with the imam it is not disliked, because it is not in the manner of competition as we have presented. And if he wishes, he does not perform supererogatory prayer, because people have a choice in it, and the best is to join as a supererogatory follower because it is prescribed in Zuhr and Isha, and if one abandons it there, perhaps he would be accused of not seeing the congregation. And it is narrated that when the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) finished Zuhr, he saw two men at the back of the rows who had not prayed with him, so he said: Bring them to me. They came trembling. He said: Take it easy, for I am the son of a woman who used to eat dried meat. Then he said: What prevented you from praying with us? They said: We had prayed in our dwellings. The Prophet said: When you pray in your dwellings, then come to the prayer of a people, pray with them, except in Asr. And if one stands for the third rak'ah, and iqamah is made before his prostration, he cuts while standing with one taslim, in the most correct view. And he said: Make your prayer with them a supererogatory one. Meaning nafl, as in al-Inayah and al-Dirayah. For it is said: Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i related from Yazid ibn al-Aswad who said: I performed Hajj with the Prophet and prayed the morning prayer with him in the Mosque of al-Khayf. When he finished, he saw two men at the back of the people who had not prayed with him. He said: Bring them to me. They came trembling. He said: What prevented you from praying with us? They said: O Messenger of Allah, we had prayed in our dwellings. He said: Do not do that. When you pray in your dwellings, then come to the mosque of a congregation, pray with them, for it is a supererogatory prayer for you. Al-Tirmidhi authenticated it. The answer is that it is contradicted by the hadith previously mentioned prohibiting supererogatory prayer after Asr and Fajr, and it is given precedence due to its greater strength, and because the preventive factor takes precedence. And there is a clear hadith related by al-Daraqutni from Ibn Umar that the Prophet said: When you pray in your family, then you find the prayer, pray it, except Fajr and Maghrib. And the command to pray in other than these two times is for recommendation, and the indicator turning the command away from obligation is making it a nafl. (Except) that one does not join as a supererogatory follower (in Asr) and Fajr due to the dislike of nafl, and its dislike in Maghrib because it necessitates opposing the imam if he completes it as four, and if he agrees with him, it necessitates performing the mutilated nafl as we will mention.
Source pages p. 468

Commentary
This passage provides detailed Hanafi rules on cutting short an optional (nafl) prayer when the congregational prayer (jama'ah) begins. The passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn, explaining the conditions and methods. The author first discusses the general case: if one has started a prayer (whether fard or nafl) and the congregation starts, the ruling depends on what one has done. If one has not yet prostrated in the first rak'ah, he may cut immediately, whether the prayer is four or non-four. If he has prostrated in a non-four-rak'ah prayer (like Fajr or Maghrib), he still cuts after prostration with a salutation, because adding another rak'ah would cause him to miss the congregation entirely, and nafl is not performed after Fajr. For Maghrib, the majority view treats it like a complete prayer, so one does not perform nafl after it as a follower. The author then specifies that these rulings apply only if one has started a fard prayer; if one is in a nafl prayer, he should complete it in pairs (shaf'an) before joining. A vowed prayer (nadhr) is treated like a fard. Additionally, the iqamah must be in the same place of performance; if iqamah is made in another mosque while he is at home or another mosque, he does not cut at all, according to al-Marghinani. The passage also covers a scenario where one is in a nafl and a funeral prayer (janazah) is about to be missed; he may cut to join the funeral because he cannot combine both merits, and the missed nafl can be made up, unlike the funeral. This implies that cutting a fard for a similar reason is also permissible. Next, the author explains the ruling for a four-rak'ah prayer: if one has already prostrated in the first rak'ah, he should add a second rak'ah, complete it with tashahhud and taslim, making those two rak'ahs a nafl, then join the congregation as a muqtadi intending fard (muftarid). If one has already prayed three rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah fard, he should complete it as four alone. There is an intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Muhammad is reported to say that he should complete it sitting to turn it into nafl, then join the congregation to combine rewards. The author favors the apparent view that the majority has the ruling of the whole, so he cannot nullify it. After completing alone, he may join as a nafl follower (mutanaffil) if he wishes, and this is better especially for Zuhr and Isha because nafl is allowed after them. The passage then provides hadith proofs: the Prophet (peace be upon him) told two men who had prayed at home to join the congregation and make their prayer supererogatory. This hadith supports the ruling. However, the author addresses an objection: another hadith (from Abu Dawud, etc.) seems to allow repeating the prayer after Fajr and Asr as nafl. The Hanafi response is that the hadith prohibiting nafl after Fajr and Asr is stronger and takes precedence, and there is also a specific hadith from al-Daraqutni exempting only Fajr and Maghrib. Thus, one does not join as a nafl follower in Asr or Fajr due to the dislike of nafl in those times, and also not in Maghrib because it would necessitate opposing the imam or performing a 'mutilated' nafl (al-batira', meaning an incomplete rakat).

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): A supererogatory (voluntary) prayer, not obligatory.
مفترض (muftarid): One who intends the obligatory prayer (fard) while following the imam.
متنفل (mutanaffil): One who prays a supererogatory prayer, especially as a follower behind an imam.
البتيراء (al-batira'): A prayer that is incomplete or 'dock-tailed', here referring to a nafl prayer of an odd number of rak'ah (e.g., one rak'ah) which is considered deficient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person is praying the sunnah of Fajr (two rak'ah) at home. The iqamah for Fajr congregation begins after he has prostrated in the first rak'ah. According to the Hanafi school, what should he do?
A) Cut with one taslim and join the congregation as a muftarid.
B) Add a second rak'ah to make it a three-rak'ah prayer, then join as a mutanaffil.
C) Complete the two rak'ahs as nafl and then join the congregation as a mutanaffil.
D) Continue praying four rak'ahs alone and then miss the congregation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi rules for cutting short a nafl prayer when congregation begins are precise: cut before prostration, complete a pair after prostration in four-rak'ah, cut after prostration in non-four, and never join as a nafl follower after Fajr, Asr, or Maghrib.

Cutting Short for Congregation: Four Hanafi Opinions on the Method
Explains the ikhtilaf on cutting short a fard prayer for congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four Hanafi opinions on how to cut short a fard prayer when the congregation starts during the third rak'ah and identify the most correct view (mufta bihi).

Core Idea
When cutting short a fard prayer for congregation, the preferred method is to remain standing and make one taslim, not return to sitting.

You start a fard prayer alone, then during the third rak'ah (before prostration) you hear the iqamah for congregation. The Hanafi school agrees you must cut short, but the exact method is debated. Four opinions exist within the school, each with its own reasoning. This lesson walks you through the ikhtilaf and helps you understand which view is most relied upon in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling of cutting short
Recognize that this applies to a person praying a four-rak'ah fard alone who is standing for the third rak'ah before prostration, and the congregation's iqamah begins. Cutting short is wajib, but the method is disputed.
The ruling is wajib, not fard, because it is based on a zanni dalil.
2
List the four opinions on the method
The text mentions four opinions, though the fourth is cut off. The first opinion (al-Halwani/Sarakhsi) is to return to sitting. The second (most correct) is to cut while standing with one taslim. The third is cut while standing with two taslims? The fourth is not specified.
Only the first two are fully discussed.
3
Examine the first opinion and its proofs
Understand why al-Halwani and al-Sarakhsi favour returning to sitting: because the two rak'ah already performed become nafl and require a sitting with tashahhud. If you do not return, the prayer is invalid. This view is recorded in al-Nawadir.
Within this opinion, there is further difference on tashahhud and taslim.
4
Examine the second opinion and its preference
The author states that cutting while standing with one taslim is al-ashahh (most correct). The reasoning is that sitting is for dissolution (tahlil) of the prayer, but this is a cut (qat'), so cutting while standing is more appropriate.
This is the mufta bihi view.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: in practice, a person in this situation should say one salam while standing and thus exit his solo prayer, then join the congregation without reciting tashahhud while standing.
No need to return to sitting.

And if one stands for the third (rak'ah) of a four-rak'ah prayer alone, and iqamah is made before his prostration (for the third), he cuts. And there is a difference of opinion on the method of cutting into four opinions: Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: He returns to sitting, and if he does not return to sitting, his prayer becomes invalid, and this is mentioned in al-Nawadir, and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi chose it, because the sitting (performed) did not occur as fard, and since his two rak'ahs have become nafl, they cannot do without the obligatory sitting, as in al-Inayah. Then when he returns to sitting, some said: he performs tashahhud a second time because the first sitting was not a closing sitting. And some said: that tashahhud suffices him, because returning to sitting nullifies the standing, as if it had not been, so this sitting is the first sitting. Then they differed on his salutation: according to some, he makes two taslims because it is the dissolving (of the prayer) from devotion; and according to some, one taslim, because the second taslim is for dissolution, and this is a cut from one aspect, as in Mi'raj al-Dirayah. And the second opinion on the method of cutting is expressed by his statement: he cuts (while standing with one taslim) (in the most correct), because sitting is for dissolution and this is cutting, likewise from

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: a person is praying the third rak'ah of a four-rak'ah fard prayer (like Zuhr, Asr, or Isha) alone, and before he prostrates for the third rak'ah, the congregation (jama'ah) begins. The Hanafi school agrees that he must cut short (qata'a) the prayer, but there is a difference of opinion (ikhtilaf) on the exact method of cutting. The author presents four opinions within the Hanafi school. The first opinion, attributed to Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani and also chosen by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, is that he should return to the sitting position (qu'ud) from the third rak'ah. If he does not return to sitting, his prayer becomes invalid. This view is recorded in al-Nawadir (the rare transmissions). The reasoning given is that the sitting he performed after the second rak'ah did not count as a fard sitting (because he had not yet completed two rak'ah of fard? Actually, the text says: 'because the sitting (performed) did not occur as fard, and since his two rak'ahs have become nafl, they cannot do without the obligatory sitting.' This seems to indicate that once he stands for the third, the prayer intention changes? The commentary in al-Inayah clarifies that the first two rak'ah become nafl, and they require a sitting with tashahhud. So he must return to sitting to complete that requirement. After returning to sitting, there is further difference: should he recite tashahhud again? Some say yes because the first tashahhud was not a closing one; others say no, because the return nullifies the standing so this sitting becomes the first sitting. Then on the salutation: some say two taslims (like a normal prayer), others say one taslim because this is a cut (qat') and the second taslim would be for dissolution which is not needed. The second opinion (which the author identifies as the most correct, al-ashahh) is that he cuts while standing with a single taslim. This is preferred because sitting is for dissolution (tahlil) but this is a cut, and cutting while standing is more appropriate. The text is cut off at the end, but it likely continues with the third and fourth opinions. The author's citation of sources (al-Nawadir, al-Inayah, Mi'raj al-Dirayah) shows the authority weight.

Key Terms
قطع (qat'): To cut short or break a prayer; specifically, to discontinue the prayer in a valid manner to join the congregation.
قعود (qu'ud): The sitting position in prayer, specifically the final sitting (qadah) for tashahhud.
تسليمة (taslimah): The salutation (saying 'assalamu alaykum') to exit prayer. One taslim is sufficient according to Hanafi; two are sunnah.
النوادر (al-Nawadir): A collection of rare transmissions from the early Hanafi imams, often containing rulings that differ from the zahir al-riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view (al-ashahh) in the Hanafi school, how should a person cut short his fard prayer when congregation starts while he is standing for the third rak'ah (before prostration)?
A) Return to the sitting position, recite tashahhud again, and make two taslims.
B) Return to sitting, make one taslim.
C) Remain standing and make one taslim.
D) Remain standing and make two taslims.

Key Takeaway
The most correct method to cut short a fard prayer when congregation starts during the third rak'ah is to say one taslim while standing, without returning to sitting.

Cutting a Supererogatory Prayer to Join the Congregation
Commentary on cutting nafl and related cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on cutting a supererogatory prayer to join the congregation and apply the mufta bihi method of cutting while standing with one taslima.

Core Idea
Cutting a nafl prayer is wajib when the congregation begins; the mufta bihi method is to cut while standing with one taslima.

When you are praying a supererogatory prayer and the congregation's iqamah is given, you must cut your prayer to join. The Hanafi school discusses several methods, but the relied-upon view is to cut while standing with a single salutation. This lesson explains that ruling, the four intra-Hanafi opinions, and also covers related cases: the sunnah of Jumu'ah/Zuhr when the congregation begins, and the special exception for the Fajr sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the general ruling
The person is praying a four-rak'ah supererogatory prayer alone, stands for the third rak'ah, and the iqamah is given before prostration. The ruling is that he must cut (qat') his prayer to join the congregation.
This ruling is based on the hadith and the need to prioritise congregational prayer.
2
Analyze the four intra-Hanafi opinions on how to cut
Four methods are presented: (1) return to sitting (al-Hulwani, al-Sarakhsi), (2) cut while standing with one taslima (the mufta bihi), (3) say takbir with intention to join the imam (Fakhr al-Islam), and (4) choice between cutting while standing or returning to sitting. Understand the reasoning behind each.
The difference stems from whether the sitting performed was sufficient and how the prayer is dissolved.
3
Apply the tarjih to determine the mufta bihi
The commentator states 'in al-ashah' (the most correct view) and relies on al-Muhit, al-'Inayah, and al-Dirayah to prefer cutting while standing with one taslima. This is the operative position for fatwa.
The key dalil: 'sitting is for dissolution (tahlil), and this is cutting from one aspect.'
4
Extend to the sunnah of Jumu'ah and Zuhr
If one started the sunnah of Jumu'ah and the khatib came out, or the sunnah of Zuhr and the iqamah was given, the sunnah is cut after two rak'ahs by giving salutation, then completed as four rak'ahs after the fard prayer.
This ruling is from Imam Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf, and it is the most appropriate because one can make up the sunnah later.
5
Handle the case of joining the congregation while having prayed sunnah
If one attends the mosque and the imam is in fard, one should join immediately and not engage in sunnah, except for the Fajr sunnah which may be prayed in the mosque if safe from missing the fard, but with detachments (behind a pillar, at the door).
The Fajr sunnah is given special treatment due to specific hadith evidence.

Except in Asr. And if he stood for the third (rak'ah), and the congregation was established before his prostration, he cuts while standing with one taslima, in the most correct view. And make your prayer with them a supererogatory prayer. That is, a nafl, as in al-'Inayah and al-Dirayah. If it is said: Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i narrated from Yazid ibn al-Aswad that he said: 'I witnessed the Hajj with the Prophet (peace be upon him) and prayed the Fajr prayer with him in the mosque of al-Khayf. When he finished his prayer, he saw two men at the back of the people who had not prayed with him. He said: Bring them to me. They were brought trembling. He said: What prevented you from praying with us? They said: O Messenger of Allah, we had prayed in our dwellings. He said: Do not do that. When you pray in your dwellings and then come to a congregational mosque, pray with them, for it will be a supererogatory prayer for you.' Al-Tirmidhi authenticated it. The answer is that it is opposed by the previous hadith forbidding supererogatory prayer after Asr and Fajr, which is given precedence due to its greater strength; and because the preventing factor is given precedence, and there is an explicit hadith narrated by al-Daraqutni from Ibn 'Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'When you pray in your family, then you catch the prayer, pray it, except Fajr and Maghrib.' The command to pray in other than these two times is for recommendation, and the factor diverting the command from obligation makes it a supererogatory prayer, except that one does not follow as a supererogatory worshipper in Asr and Fajr due to the dislike of supererogatory prayer, and its dislike in Maghrib because it would necessitate opposing the imam if he completed it as four, and if he agrees with him, it necessitates performing supererogatory prayer with the 'cut-off' (al-batira') as we will mention. And if he stood for the third (rak'ah) of a four-rak'ah prayer alone, and the congregation was established before his prostration for the third, he cuts. There is disagreement on how to cut into four opinions: Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani said: He returns to sitting, and if he does not return to sitting, his prayer becomes invalid, and that is mentioned in al-Nawadir, and it was chosen by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi; because the sitting performed did not occur as obligatory, and his two rak'ahs, having changed to supererogatory, could not avoid the obligatory sitting. Then when he returns to sitting, some said he performs a second tashahhud because the first sitting was not a sitting of completion, and some said that the tashahhud suffices him because the return to sitting nullifies the standing as if it had not been, so this sitting is the first sitting. Then they differed about his salutation: some said he gives two taslimas because it is a dissolution from the act of worship, and some said one taslima because the second taslima is for dissolution, and this is cutting from one aspect. The second opinion on how to cut is stated by him: he cuts while standing with one taslima, in the most correct view, because sitting is for dissolution and this is cutting, as in al-Muhit. The third opinion, said Fakhr al-Islam: the most correct is that he says the takbir while standing because he concludes his prayer, so when he says the takbir standing with the intention to enter into the imam's prayer, the first prayer is cut within the context of entering into the imam's prayer. Then he has the choice: if he wishes, he raises his hands, and if he wishes, he does not raise them, as in al-'Inayah. The fourth opinion is that he has the choice between cutting while standing and returning to sitting, as stated in al-Dirayah, and also in al-Muhit. And if he had started the sunnah of Jumu'ah and the khatib came out, or he started the sunnah of Zuhr and the congregation was established, he gives the salutation after sitting at the end of two rak'ahs. This is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on them), and it is the most appropriate; because he is able to make it up later, as he indicated by saying: Then he performs the sunnah as four rak'ahs with one taslima after finishing the obligatory prayer and what follows. There is no invalidation in giving the salutation at the end of two rak'ahs, so the obligation of listening and performing in the most complete manner is not missed without cause. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi and al-Baqqali inclined toward this view. It was also said: He completes it as four, and al-Asl referred to this because it is one prayer, as in al-Fath. A group of mashayikh authenticated that he completes it as four, as in the commentary of 'Allamah al-Maqdisi. And whoever attends (other than Fajr prayer, as we will mention) and the imam is in the obligatory prayer, he follows him and does not occupy himself with the sunnah in the mosque, even if he has not missed anything. If he is able to perform the sunnah before the imam bows outside the mosque, he does so to acquire both excellences. And if he fears missing one rak'ah, he joins him, as in al-Tabyin. Except in Fajr, for he prays the sunnah, even in the mosque, but far from the row, praying them at the door of the mosque if there is a place for that, otherwise in the mosque behind the rows by a pillar. The most disliked is that he prays intermingled with the row, opposing the congregation. Next in dislike is that he is behind the row without a barrier between him and the row, as in al-Bada'i'. This is if he is safe from missing him, i.e., missing the imam by catching up even in the tashahhud, because he obtains the virtue of congregation by it. His statement in al-Tajnis: 'The apparent in the madhhab is that if he fears missing two rak'ahs, he joins the imam.' Perhaps its basis is the statement of Muhammad concerning Jumu'ah that one does not catch it except by catching one rak'ah with the imam. Because al-Kamal said: 'The correct view is that our three imams agree that he prays the Fajr sunnah here, i.e., if he does not catch the imam in the tashahhud.' We have verified it in Hashiyah al-Durar, praise be to Allah. The Fajr sunnah is specified with this because it is narrated that he returned from the peace...
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from Imdad al-Fattah on Nur al-Idah, dealing with the ruling on cutting a supererogatory prayer to join the congregation. It begins by noting the exception of Asr and Fajr where one does not follow the imam as a supererogatory worshipper due to the prohibition of nafl after those prayers. Then it addresses the situation of a person who is praying a four-rak'ah nafl alone and stands for the third rak'ah when the congregation's iqamah is given before he prostrates. The relied-upon ruling (al-ashah) is that he cuts the prayer while standing by giving one taslima. The author then discusses four differing opinions among Hanafi scholars on how to cut: (1) returning to sitting (al-Hulwani, al-Sarakhsi), (2) cutting while standing with one taslima (the mufta bihi), (3) saying takbir while standing with intention to join (Fakhr al-Islam), and (4) choice between cutting while standing or returning to sitting. Next, the sunnah of Jumu'ah when the khatib comes out and the sunnah of Zuhr when iqamah is given: the view of Abu Hanifah and Abu Yusuf is to give salutation after two rak'ahs, then perform the sunnah four rak'ahs after the fard. Finally, for one who attends while the imam is in fard, he joins immediately and does not engage in sunnah, except for the Fajr sunnah which he may pray even in the mosque if he is safe from missing the fard, but with detachments. The proof for the permissibility of repeated prayer as nafl is the hadith of Yazid ibn al-Aswad, but it is countered by the stronger prohibition of nafl after Asr and Fajr. The command in the hadith is interpreted as recommendatory, as made clear by the explicit exceptions in the hadith of Ibn 'Umar.

Key Terms
نافلة (nafila): A supererogatory prayer, voluntary act of worship beyond the obligatory.
قطع (qat'): Cutting or discontinuing a prayer before completion.
قعدة (qa'da): The sitting posture in prayer, specifically the final sitting (qa'da akhira) or the first sitting.
تسليمة (taslima): The salutation at the end of prayer, saying 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' to the right and left.
بتيراء (al-batira'): A supererogatory prayer that is 'cut off' or incomplete, such as Maghrib performed as nafl with only three rak'ahs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi), how should a person cut a four-rak'ah supererogatory prayer when the congregation's iqamah is given while he is standing for the third rak'ah?
A) Return to the sitting position and give two taslimas.
B) Cut while standing by giving one taslima.
C) Say takbir with the intention to join the imam.
D) He may choose between cutting while standing or returning to sitting.

Key Takeaway
When the congregation begins, cut your nafl prayer while standing with one taslima; for the sunnah of Jumu'ah/Zuhr, cut after two rak'ahs; and for Fajr, pray your sunnah separately if you can catch the fard.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Leaving Sunnah of Fajr to Join Congregation When Fearing Missing the Imam
Ruling on preferring congregation over Sunnah of Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the Sunnah of Fajr to join the congregation and explain the proof based on the greater reward of congregation.

Core Idea
Congregation’s reward outweighs the Sunnah of Fajr.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: a person is performing the Sunnah of Fajr and fears he will miss the congregational Fajr prayer. The Hanafi school gives clear guidance on which act takes precedence. We will examine the ruling, its proof, and the underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The ruling is that one should leave the Sunnah of Fajr and join the congregation if he fears missing the imam.
This is a matter of preference between two sunnah mu'akkadah acts.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The reward of congregation is greater: 27 times the reward of praying alone. Also, severe warnings against leaving congregation are cited from hadith.
Dalil includes comparison of rewards and hadith about hypocrisy and cursing.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the proof show the ruling? Congregation is an intrinsic completion (mukammila dhatiyya) of the obligatory prayer, while Sunnah is extrinsic. The obligatory prayer in congregation is superior to any Sunnah.
The 27-fold multiplication applies to the obligatory prayer, not to the Sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Some schools may prioritize the Sunnah of Fajr, but the Hanafi position is to prefer congregation.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on different weightings of evidence.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon? The mufta bihi is to leave the Sunnah and join the congregation, as supported by the texts cited.
The author references al-Fath, al-Diraya, and Jami' Abu al-Mu'in.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن لم يأمن تَرَكَها. واقتدى بالإمام؛ لأن ثواب الجماعة أعظم، فإن الجماعة مكملة ذاتية للفرائض، والسنة مكملة خارجية عنها ، فيرتكب الأرجح، وفضيلة الفرض بجماعة أعظم من فضيلة ركعتي الفجر؛ لأنها تفضل [ الفرض ] منفرداً بسبع وعشرين ضعفاً؛ لا تبلغ ركعتا الفجر ضعفاً واحداً منها، لأنها أضعاف الفرض، كذا في «الفتح» ، فتكون الصلاة بالجماعة كسـبع وعشرين فرضاً عند عند الانفراد، وكل فرض أعظم ثواباً من السنة فالمجموع أولى، كذا في « الدراية» عـن جــامـع أبي المعين انتهى. والوعيد على الترك للجماعة ألزم منه على ركعتي الفجر، وهو مـا تقـدم فـي بـاب الإمامة من قول أبي مسعود : « لا يتخلف عنها إلا منافق »، وما قدمناه مـن أنـه [ هَـمَّ ] بِتَحْرِيقِ بُيُوتِ المُتَخَلَّفِينَ ) () وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام : « تَارِكُ الجَمَاعَةِ مَلْعُونٌ فِي التَّوْرَاةِ والإنجيل والفُرْقَانِ ) كذا في ( الدراية».
And if he does not feel safe (from missing the Imam), he leaves it (the Sunnah of Fajr). And he follows the Imam because the reward of congregation is greater; indeed, congregation is an intrinsic completion of the obligatory prayers, while the Sunnah is an extrinsic completion. So the more preponderant is adopted. And the virtue of performing an obligatory prayer in congregation is greater than the virtue of the two rak'ahs of Fajr because it surpasses the obligatory prayer performed alone by twenty-seven times. The two rak'ahs of Fajr do not reach even one time of that, because they are multiples of the obligatory prayer. Thus, prayer in congregation is like twenty-seven obligatory prayers performed alone, and every obligatory prayer is greater in reward than the Sunnah, so the combined is superior. So in al-Diraya from Jami' Abu al-Mu'in. And the threat of punishment for leaving congregation is more binding than that for leaving the two rak'ahs of Fajr. That is what has been stated in the chapter of imamah from the statement of Abu Mas'ud: 'None stays behind from it except a hypocrite,' and what we mentioned that he intended to burn the houses of those who stayed behind, and he, peace be upon him, said: 'The one who leaves congregation is cursed in the Torah, the Gospel, and the Criterion.' So in al-Diraya.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses a situation where one is performing the Sunnah of Fajr and fears that if he continues, he will miss the congregation. The ruling is clear: he should leave the Sunnah and join the Imam because the reward of congregation is far greater. The commentary explains the reasoning: congregation is an intrinsic completion (mukammila dhatiyya) of the obligatory prayer, while the Sunnah is an extrinsic completion (mukammila kharijiyya). The obligatory prayer in congregation is superior to the Sunnah by a factor of twenty-seven times the reward of the obligatory prayer alone, while the Sunnah of Fajr does not even reach that. The threat of punishment for abandoning congregation is more severe than for abandoning the Sunnah of Fajr, as evidenced by hadith. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).

Key Terms
سنّة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of Sunnah prayer before the obligatory Fajr prayer.
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): The congregational prayer performed behind an imam.
فضل (fadl): Virtue or additional reward beyond the original act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a person do if while performing the Sunnah of Fajr he fears missing the congregational prayer?
A) Complete the Sunnah and then join the congregation later.
B) Break the Sunnah and join the congregation immediately.
C) Continue the Sunnah and pray alone afterwards.
D) Ask the imam to wait for him.

Key Takeaway
When fearing missing the congregation, leave the Sunnah of Fajr and join the Imam, as congregational reward surpasses the Sunnah.
